By the time she was dressed – in her T-shirt, leggings, and Rio’s hoodie – Agatha’s legs felt a bit sore from all the stumbling around. And she hadn’t even made it to the kitchen yet. Thankfully, Lilia still had the wheelchair from the hospital. She had Agatha sit down and pushed her out of the bedroom and toward a table, where she had laid out a small spread of food.

Agatha couldn’t name a single thing she’d eaten that morning, but it was all delicious and it all sat heavy in her stomach as Lilia walked her down the street toward the marketplace – the plaza, she called it – about an hour later. She had tied Agatha’s now-clean hair into a braid after breakfast when it kept falling in front of her face as she shoveled scrambled eggs into her face. She had never eaten eggs before, but they were quite possibly the best thing she’d ever tasted. Way better than eel.

And they were hot, like the water had been. Hot food was so good!

Hot sun? Not as good.

Agatha’s face felt hot like it did when she blushed, but not in a good or even an embarrassing way. It felt bad. It made water appear at her hairline. Agatha reached up to wipe the water away, but it just kept coming.

“You need to take that hoodie off, doll,” Lilia said, “or you’re going to overheat and pass out.”

“But—” Agatha started to protest.

“No buts,” Lilia said. “You can keep it in your lap if you want, but it should not be wrapped around your body when it’s already ninety degrees out.”

She helped Agatha tug the sweater off and fold it onto her lap, where it stayed for the rest of their journey to the plaza.

When they got there, there were already a lot of people milling about. A few of them waved at Lilia and greeted her by name. Obviously, she was rather well-known in her community. Lilia waved back as she continued to push Agatha toward one of the structures in the plaza.

It was called a thrift store, Lilia told her. It was a place where one could buy articles of clothing with which to adorn their body. There were many different articles to choose from; Agatha just needed to find the ones that suited her.

“Why do…humans…wear…clothes?” Agatha asked, still leaking water from her hairline. There was some underneath her arms, as well, though Lilia had claimed to put some kind of soap there earlier that she promised would keep that from happening. “Mermaids…don’t.”

“Very good speaking there, sport,” Lilia said, patting her shoulder. “Humans need protection from the elements,” she whispered as they entered the store, which was buzzing less than the outside. “The sun can burn our skin, and sometimes it gets too cold to bare all. I thought it was strange the first time I saw clothes, too,” she admitted. “But then I started to pick out my own to wear, and…well…it’s fun.”

“Fun?” Agatha asked, snorting in disbelief. “How?”

“There are a lot of different kinds of shirts and skirts and dresses,” Lilia said, “with a lot of different patterns. I like expressing myself with different colors. My tail was yellow and orange when I lived in the Pod, but here…oh, there are so many different colors I can wear. I can change them every day or wear them all at once. The possibilities are endless! You’ll see.”

She wheeled Agatha to a section where many different articles of clothing were hanging on metal tubes.

“What is your favorite color?” Lilia asked as she started rifling through a collection of T-shirts.

“My tail…was purple…and teal,” Agatha said. “I…liked the…purple more.”

“Noted,” Lilia said. “You’ve really caught on to talking when you take your time. How does it feel?”

“Wrong,” Agatha said. “I…don’t like it.”

“You’ll get used to it,” Lilia hummed, draping some articles of purple over her arm. “We should get you some real shoes while we’re at it.” She looked down at Agatha’s feet, upon which she’d placed “flip-flops” which were odd pieces of lime green foam held to her feet with Y-shaped plastic. Agatha had seen similar shoes on other people’s feet as they walked.

She didn’t like these, either.

“We’ll find you some good ones, don’t worry,” Lilia said. “Now let’s go try these on, huh?”

“Try on?” Agatha asked.

“To make sure that they fit,” Lilia explained, “and that you like them.”

Agatha groaned. “Can’t we just…buy them and…leave?”

She was getting better at this talking thing.

“Nope!” Lilia chirped, patting her head as she started wheeling her deeper into the store.

In the end, trying out clothes wasn’t really all that bad.

The tiny room the store employee had unlocked for them had a bench so Agatha didn’t need to worry about the wheelchair anymore. And it was big enough that Lilia could enter and help her try on her clothes.

When Agatha didn’t find anything that fit with that first batch, Lilia adjusted and went out to find new clothes.

When she came back, she had a couple of skirts, a pair of jeans, and some kind of…well, Agatha didn’t know what to call it.

It was like the shorts that Lilia had found, but it had a top part, as well. The top part was made of slightly different, stretchy material in the back that went over Agatha’s shoulders and attached to the front by two buttons, Lilia had called them. The stretchier part had more colors than the rest of the article, but Agatha liked that a lot.

Agatha would have gladly worn the overalls (again, Lilia’s word) without one, but Lilia forced her to put on a light purple shirt beneath them. On the front of the overalls was what Lilia called a pocket, where Agatha could put things she wanted to hold onto.

There were two more at her hips, which she immediately stuck her hands into. The material on the inside was smoother than the rough denim they were made of. Agatha looked at herself in the mirror and liked what she saw. The overalls fit her body much better than anything else, and they were the first article of clothing that she really liked.

“I want this,” she told Lilia. “Can I have it?”

“Of course,” Lilia affirmed. “It’s what we’re here for, and those are only ten dollars. You have to get a few more things, though. And then we’re going next door to find you some underwear. That one pair I had in your size is not going to be enough for the week. Ooh! And a bathing suit for your PT. Rio said you’re going into a pool today.”

“Pool?” Agatha asked, furrowing her brow.

“Like a big bathtub,” Lilia said. “Or a small ocean, I guess. No saltwater, though. Also, it’s not typically warm, but I don’t know if this one will be. It’s at the hospital, so it might be heated.”

“I’m going to…swim?” Agatha asked.

“Maybe,” Lilia said. “We can get you a cheap bathing suit next door at Russo’s.”

“Why not here?”

“Doll, trust me when I tell you that you do not want a thrift store bathing suit,” Lilia said. “Or underwear. Now let’s try something else on.”

By the time they were done shopping, Agatha had three full bags of clothing to wear until she could go home. She had bought a few T-shirts that had nice patterns on them as well as a few with funny sayings. She had her overalls, a few pairs of shorts, a skirt, a dress that she liked to twirl in, a pair of sandals that felt better on her feet, and a pair of purple sneakers that Lilia had found in her size. At Russo’s, she got some socks, a 10-pack of underwear, and two bathing suits because Lilia said there was a sale.

When they finally left, the sun was higher in the sky and hotter than before. Lilia pulled out her strange rectangle and let out a low whistle.

“It’s nearly a hundred degrees already,” she said, “and it’s not even noon yet. Are you hungry?”

Agatha’s stomach began to growl as if on cue.

“I’ll take that as a yes,” Lilia cackled. “There’s a diner right over there. We can get ourselves an early lunch.”

“Scrambled eggs?” Agatha asked.

“That’s more of a breakfast food,” Lilia informed her, “but I don’t see why you can’t have some for lunch, too.”

“What do you have…for lunch?” Agatha asked.

“How about I order you the best burger you’ve ever had in your life?” Lilia suggested as she wheeled Agatha across the street to another structure. Through the large windows, she could see people sitting and talking and laughing while others walked around, holding large round disks with cups full of liquid and plates filled with various foods.

The sight made Agatha’s mouth water, but the smell as soon as they entered made her stomach growl even harder.

“I think…I’d like that,” Agatha said even though she had no idea what a burger was.

Agatha's about to have her world rocked.

Chapter 6

Chapter Summary

Rio starts to work with the pretty girl she caught in her fishing net.

Chapter Six

Rio liked her job. She did. Sometimes, she even loved her job. Some of her patients were pretty chill even though they were usually in a decent amount of pain.

But some were just straight up assholes for no reason.

Like Tony.

Tony was a perfect example of an asshole whether he was in pain or not. He had a lot of money, so he wasn’t dependent on his insurance to pay for his physical therapy, and he acted like that meant he had every right to curse Rio out whenever he got frustrated. And he thought that Rio would be forced to take it just because he was paying for her services out of pocket.

Nope.

“Look,” Tony huffed, still sitting on the ground where Rio had left him, nearly twenty minutes ago, “I said I was sorry. Can we please get back to it now?”

“Nope,” Rio said, scrolling on her phone. There were a few cute shark videos that she double-tapped on her Insta and a text from Alice about how she couldn’t get the stench of trout off of her hands.

Rio: then try not catching trout with your bare hands next time, dweeb!

Alice: you’re so mean to me!

Alice: i’m gonna get eddie to form a union w me!

Rio: do u kno how many fisherman there are in this town?

Rio: i could replace both of you in no time

Alice: wow…after twenty years of friendship

Alice: u treat me like this

Alice: wut would the sharks think of u?

Alice: WHY WON’T THE SMELL COME OFF?!?!

Rio snorted and lowered her phone when she heard grunting. She glanced up to see Tony attempting to pull himself up by the parallel bars, but his legs were unwilling to hold any of his weight. He kept falling and flailing, and he looked and sounded like he was about to start crying.

Rio watched him struggle for a few more minutes before it legitimately got too pathetic for her to stomach any longer. Then she sighed, tucked her phone into the pocket of her athletic shorts, and stood.

She took her time walking over to him, letting him sweat for a few seconds longer than necessary before she crouched behind him, placing her arms under his and lifting with her knees – which, hilariously, coaxed a girlish squeal out of him in surprise.

Rio tried, and failed, not to snicker as she helped him to his feet. Tony grabbed onto the parallel bars to keep himself standing as Rio pulled his chair over, once again taking her sweet time to let him sweat it out. As soon as it touched the back of his calves, however, he collapsed into it, sweaty and panting.

“Now what did we learn?” Rio sing-songed as she wheeled Tony out from between the bars.

Stubbornly, Tony crossed his arms over his chest, refusing to answer the question.

Rio started to tilt the wheelchair forward, threatening to spill him back onto the ground.

“Wait, wait, wait!” he protested. “I’m sorry! I’m sorry!”

“Sorry for…?”

“Calling you a heinous cunt with a God complex!” Stark practically squealed like a pig. Rio could swear she saw tears rolling down his cheeks as he clung to the chair. He would definitely swear that it was sweat later on, but Rio knew the truth.

She’d let him have a tiny bit of his dignity though she didn’t think he deserved it.

She set the wheels of his chair back down and stepped away, giving Tony the opportunity to roll away from her like the pussy he was. And, of course, he did this just as there was a knock on the door and it opened, revealing his wife, Pepper, poking her head in, a toddler on her hip.

“Hey!” she said. “Sorry we’re late! There was traffic.” She placed the toddler on the floor, and she ran straight into her father’s arms, squealing as he showered her face in kisses.

For all his faults and assholery, Tony Stark was at least a decent dad.

“How was your PT?” Pepper asked, walking up to run her fingers through his spiky hair. “Looks like you worked up quite a sweat.” She wiped her hand on her skirt.

“She is insane,” Tony huffed to Pepper, clutching his daughter to his chest.

“Who? Morgan? Yeah, she skipped her nap today,” Pepper said.

“No!” Tony huffed. “My princess is perfect!” He kissed his daughter’s forehead. “I’m talking about that,” he pointed to Rio, who gave him a bored expression in response, “lunatic! She let me struggle on the ground for over twenty minutes, begging for help!”

“Well, what did you do to her?” Pepper asked, taking note of Rio’s unbothered expression.

“I didn’t do anything!” Tony insisted.

“I have cameras,” Rio informed him.

“I may have lost my temper a little bit,” he admitted.

“Mhm,” Pepper said, turning to Rio. “What did he call you?”

Rio eyed the tiny child sitting in her father’s lap, showing off a Barney Band-Aid wrapped around her pointer finger. “I can’t tell you the exact word he used,” she said, “but it started with a C.”

“You had it coming,” Pepper said to her husband. “Maybe next time, you’ll think before you yell insults at somebody trying to help you.”

“But, I—”

“No buts,” Pepper said, walking around behind him and taking hold of the back of the wheelchair. She started pushing it toward the door. “Thank you, Rio,” she said. “We’ll see you tomorrow!”

“No, we will not!” Tony insisted. “I’m never coming back to that quack! She almost killed me!”

“Tony, she’s the only PT on the island,” Pepper reminded him. “Just grow up and shut up.”

“But Pepper!” Tony moaned as the door shut behind them.

Rio snickered and shook her head as she set about cleaning the room for her next client, who would be…

She checked the schedule on her phone and felt her face flush at the name on her screen: Agatha

The woman that had gotten caught just yesterday in her net. The pretty woman with the eyes like the ocean. The woman who had no recollection of who she was or where she was from or really anything except her first name. The woman that Rio was now tasked to teach how to walk and talk and pretty much anything else that her TBI had taken from her.

The pretty woman that Rio hadn’t really stopped thinking about in the last twenty-four hours since she first laid eyes on her.

It was embarrassing, frankly, how much space Agatha had taken up in Rio’s conscious thoughts – and even her unconscious ones – over the last twenty-four hours.

She had even dreamt about the woman the night before. She had dreamed about fishing on her boat, with an actual rod and line, and reeling it in to find Agatha hanging off a surprisingly sturdy line, smiling at her with her long brown hair flowing in the wind, looking like the cover of a trashy sapphic romance novel. Rio had swallowed thickly as her dream self leaned against the side of the boat, closer to Agatha, who also leaned in. At some point, the fishing rod had disappeared, leaving Agatha floating in mid-air. Neither of them had questioned it, however, as their noses brushed and Rio was hypnotized by Agatha’s long lashes and pouty lips and…her tail?

Dream Rio had done the smallest double-take at the tail at the end of Agatha’s body, where her legs should have been. Apparently, kissing Agatha’s lips had taken precedence over analyzing the reason why the other woman was suddenly half-fish.

Unfortunately, Rio never really got that far as her alarm began blaring milliseconds before her lips would have touched Dream Agatha’s, jarring her into the conscious world with a gasp.

Thankfully, Rio had chilled out considerably since then. They’d caught three or four large netfuls of fish with Eddie and got back to shore just before noon since Rio had her first appointment with a client at one PM and needed to grab a quick shower so that she didn’t show up smelling like fish (again).

Then came her contentious session with the spoiled rich manchild.

Now…Agatha.

Rio prided herself on her ability to keep things professional with all of her patients. It didn’t hurt that many of them were either elderly or male. The few that were not were typically straight/married women or children. The one or two single, queer, non-straight women were way more interested in getting better with Rio’s help than in forming any kind of romantic bond, which was more than okay with Rio herself.

She was good at her job. She was encouraging and firm and just the right level of unhinged to keep the more difficult patients (like Stark) in line. She was also the only PT on the island, but she had patients who took the ferry from nearby islands just to work with her sometimes.

She wasn’t hurting for work, by any means. It was what made her more willing to take on pro-bono patients, like Agatha, for whom they had no insurance information – or any information at all. Rio was all too happy to help her out, like she had done for a few other friends of Lilia. Lilia was the kind of kooky old lady to take in strays, helping out those who were down on their luck, trying to give them a second chance. A lot of them, she said, were refugees from other islands who fled their homes and were either injured in the journey or left when they couldn’t afford the astronomical medical costs for injuries and ailments they already had before they left.

None of them, however, had ever intrigued her like Agatha had.

Maybe it was because of how they’d first met, or maybe it was because she reminded Rio of the mermaids her father used to tell her about.

“Their beauty, mija, is beyond compare.”

“Are they more beautiful than Mami?”

“Ha! Nobody is more beautiful than your mami…please tell her I said that.”

Rio snorted at the memory. Her father had waxed poetic about mermaids her entire childhood as if he truly believed they existed, but Rio had stopped believing relatively early on. She honestly didn’t know if she ever truly believed in them at all.

It was a nice fantasy, though, especially when she realized that she leaned more toward the fairer sex in her teen years.

Her father had one story he would always tell about being saved from drowning by a beautiful, green-eyed, tan-skinned woman with a tail that glittered like diamonds in the sunlight. The way he painted the picture of the mermaid with his words always entranced Rio, and she could almost see the woman he described as he regaled her with stories of the whirlwind romance in his teen years.

It helped that he was more or less just describing her mother, who would be within earshot and would roll her eyes over his shoulder, making faces of disbelief that made Rio giggle.

Still, it was a nice thought. To be out at sea and see a beautiful, magical woman and have her be as entranced by Rio as Rio was by her…it was a dream.

Maybe that was why Rio had dreamt of Agatha like that: her mind had simply melded the mermaid fantasy with the reality of finding an actual woman, injured and concussed, at sea. It was very fucked up of her brain to do to her, to be entirely honest, especially when her dry spell was going on two years now.

Yeah, that’s it, Rio decided as she left the tiny gym and started heading toward the indoor pool, where she was meant to meet Lilia and Agatha. I just need to get laid or something. Not by my patient.

No matter how heart-stoppingly beautiful her eyes are.

Rio was a professional. She could keep it in her pants – or swim trunks.

Whatever.

The pool area was empty, thankfully. Not many people used it these days. It was mainly a place for patients with physical needs. There were four lanes at one end of the pool to swim laps, but the other end only went to about five feet deep and was used as a tool to help some of the hospital patients with limited mobility. It helped them walk around with limited strain on their joints.

Rio typically used it the most with her patients, but she was far from the only one. Some of the ortho doctors brought their recovering patients down to work out new joints or the cardio doctors brought their patients to give them low-stress workouts. There was usually little overlap in their schedules.

By the time Rio had set up the aqua walker next to the ramp that led into the pool on one side, it was nearing Agatha’s appointment time: 3:30pm.

Rio wanted to dive into the water immediately at the deep end. Maybe a few laps back and forth would both cool her down and give her a legitimate reason for why her heart was pounding so hard already when the woman herself hadn’t even shown up yet.

Rio swallowed thickly as she tried to focus on what the plan was for the session. Agatha was coming in to relearn how to walk after her traumatic brain injury. This was the easiest way for her to begin. Rio had made sure to set up several appointments over the next few days to achieve that goal in as little time as possible, as she had done for so many of Aunt Lilia’s other friends in the past.

It never took more than three or four days, which would be considered a miracle for most. In her classes, Rio had learned that it took most patients about six months to regain their mobility after significant trauma, but Lilia’s friends all seemed to be rockstars, practically sprinting by the time they reached that fourth day.

It got to a point where Rio didn’t even question it anymore.

She doubted Agatha would be very much different even if she wasn’t typically the kind of patient Rio saw from Lilia. All of her scans were clear, as were her blood tests, so it stood to reason that she’d be back on her feet – literally and metaphorically – in no time.

“We’re here!”

Aunt Lilia’s voice startled Rio out of her thoughts as the doors to the pool room slid open and Agatha was wheeled in, still using the chair that Marisol had given her a few days prior. She was no longer wearing the hoodie that Rio had loaned her the other day. Instead, she had on a light blue tank top and a pair of navy cotton shorts. She also had on a pair of lime green flip flops.

And her hair was pulled back from her face in a braid.

She looked so pretty.

Rio was fucked.

Lilia had a canvas bag on her shoulder that she handed off to Rio as she pressed a big, smacking kiss to her cheek in greeting. Rio flushed bright pink, feeling like a little kid in front of the girl she had a crush on as Agatha smiled at them, lifting her eyebrows.

“Lilia…” she grumbled. “I’m at work.”

“So?” Lilia huffed. “You can’t kiss your auntie hello? I changed your diapers, you know!”

“Yes, Aunt Lilia, I know,” Rio said, her voice still low as if praying Lilia would match it.

She did not.

“And you peed on me that one time, too!” Her voice echoed around the room, and Rio was struck with the sudden urge to walk straight into the pool and let herself drown. She was sure that Agatha would understand.

She heard the other woman giggle.

“So,” Lilia continued, as if she hadn’t just stabbed her ‘beloved niece’ in the back with the dagger of utter embarrassment (not to be dramatic), “what do you have planned today?”

“Same as always,” Rio replied, taking the canvas back over to a bench sitting against the wall. She placed it down and turned back to Lilia and Agatha: “Just going for a few laps in the shallow end.” She turned to look at Agatha specifically, and found her staring, wide-eyed at the pool. It wasn’t anywhere near Olympic-sized, but it took up about seventy percent of the room they were in. “Is that okay, Agatha?” she asked. “If you don’t want to get in the water, then we can move to the gym. It may take a bit longer, but—”

“The water is fine,” Agatha said.

Rio’s eyes widened at that. She can talk?!

“We’ve been working on her speech,” Lilia said as if reading Rio’s mind – and oh-so-subtle expression. “She’s doing pretty well, I think.” She used one finger under Rio’s chin, pushing it up to meet the rest of her jaw. “You’ll catch flies, dear,” she said, teasingly.

Rio swatted her hand away and gave her a glare as she cleared her throat. She turned back to Agatha, who was once again looking at the pool.

“Are you sure you’re okay with it?” she asked. “I know, after what you’ve been through, it might not be easy to just go back into the water.”

“Rio, honey,” Lilia said, “she’ll be fine. Trust me. Half the people I’ve sent you had water-related trauma. Besides, Agatha did just fine in the bath this morning; this will be nothing for her.”

Rio mentally waved off the image of Agatha in the bathtub, feeling very much like a perv for even allowing it in the first place, and made her way toward the woman still sitting in her wheelchair, grabbing the aqua walker on her way.

“You ready?” she asked, setting it up in front of Agatha’s wheelchair, within reach.

“Take those clothes off of her first, dear,” Lilia reminded her. Rio’s cheeks once again bloomed pink as her traitorous brain conjured up another image before she was mentally able to wave it away.

Now, it would likely be seared into the inside of her eyelids whenever she closed her eyes. Stupid visual imagination.

She swallowed thickly when Agatha immediately tugged off the tank top she was wearing, revealing the top half of a pretty mundane bathing suit and some sunburned shoulders.

“Oof,” Rio said, grimacing sympathetically. “Did you guys spend some time in the sun today?”

“Not that much,” Lilia said. “She just has very sensitive skin, it seems. I should have known just based on how pale she is.”

Agatha glared at Lilia over her shoulder as she tossed the tank top at her. “That sounds…like an insult,” she said, her words slow and measured. She was obviously still struggling to speak, but she was honestly doing better than many of the patients Rio had worked with who’d been afflicted with aphasia.

Good for her.

“I would never, doll,” Lilia assured her, easily catching the tank top and folding it in mid-air. She placed it onto the bench. “Your fair skin is beautiful if a bit finicky in the sun. A little aloe will fix that right up.”

Agatha rolled her eyes and Rio saw her cheeks get redder under the sunburn as she reached for the waistband of her shorts. Rio’s cheeks must have matched if the heat in her face meant anything.

She backed up, giving Agatha some space to lift her hips and get the shorts off, then helped to take them the rest of the way off, doing anything she could to think of several, decidedly unsexy things as she did so.

Dead puppies. Dead kittens. Dead sharks.

She ended up taking Agatha’s flip flops, too, tossing everything in Lilia’s general direction but unable to keep her eyes off of Agatha.

Her bathing suit was not sexy at all. It was dark blue and one piece, with a solid lighter blue triangle shape around her waist. The brand name was over Agatha’s left breast – not that Rio was looking there at all, no.

She cleared her throat and got out of her crouching position, offering her hands to Agatha. “Ready?” she asked, her voice cracking on the singular word like she was a prepubescent teenage boy. She cleared her throat, flushing.

Agatha nodded and took her hands, allowing Rio to help her up onto shaky legs.

Her gait was awkward, to say the least, as Rio helped to situate her at the aqua walker, guiding her on where to put her hands and how to lean on it with her forearms. She made sure Agatha was secure before stepping around behind her and placing her hands on her lower back, encouraging her to walk forward down the wide ramp that led into the shallow end of the pool.

“Okay,” Rio said in a low voice, “take a few steps forward.”

Agatha lifted her leg too high and ended up knocking it against her own elbow, which pushed her arm forward too quickly, which made the wheels on the aqua walker lurch forward several inches, which nearly ended up making Agatha fall flat on her face before Rio could catch her, wrapping her arms around her waist.

“Whoa!” she exclaimed, catching Agatha’s waist with one arm and using the opposite hand to keep the aqua walker close by. “Maybe we should have started further into the water.”

“Ya think?” Lilia said, peering at them over the edge of her book.

Rio glared at her. “You can leave now,” she said. “We’ll be okay.”

“You sure about that, kid? I don’t want you drowning my ward or injuring her any further.”

“We’ll be fine, Aunt Lilia!” Rio huffed. “I know how to do my job. I’ve done it before, haven’t I?”

“If you insist,” Lilia murmured, standing up with her book. “Agatha, dear, I’m going to run to the grocery store, but I’ll be back in exactly one hour, okay? Good luck, kids.”

She winked at Rio, who frowned at her.

Crazy old bat.

(Rio loved her aunt, she swore.)

Lilia left with her book, the closing of the doors echoing around the big room.

“Okay,” Rio said, guiding Agatha forward while using herself as a support for the other woman until she could reach the aqua walker. “Let’s try this again.”

She felt Agatha’s deep breath against her chest and bit her lip.

Dead sharks. Dead sharks. Dead sharks.

You are a professional.

DEAD. SHARKS.

“Take a few steps forward,” she urged, pushing lightly on Agatha’s waist. “It may be difficult at first, but it will get easier the deeper you go.”

That’s what she said.

Shut up, you idiot!

Oh great, Rio thought with a soft huff, I’m talking to myself. In my own dumb brain.

Agatha stumbled a little bit as she stepped into the water, but her legs didn’t completely fail her as she kept her weight partly on the aqua walker and partly on Rio’s arms. Rio’s hands rested lightly on her hips as she encouraged her to continue forward until the water level rose just over her waist.

“Okay,” Rio said, “great job!” She stepped away from Agatha and let herself float around her so that the aqua walker was now between them. Then she stood up, bouncing lightly on her feet. “How do you feel? Are your legs feeling okay?”

“My legs are fine,” Agatha said in that slow, measured way. “Why wouldn’t they be?”

“Most of my patients,” Rio explained, “after a TBI, still take a little time to get used to being upright, even in water. But I’ve noticed that most of Lilia’s wards typically bounce back more quickly. It helps that your scans were clean, too, I guess.”

“Scans?” Agatha asked, furrowing her brow.

“Yeah,” Rio said. “The scans of your brain. The MRI and CT scans? Didn’t anybody talk to you about them?”

“I vagly—ahem, vague-ly remember that,” Agatha said. “But I don’t think I un-undersh—” she took a deep, frustrated breath.

“It’s alright,” Rio said, gently, placing her hand over Agatha’s on the walker, “take your time. Aphasia is a bitch.”

“Aph—what?” Agatha asked, squinting at her.

“Aphasia,” Rio repeated. “It’s when you lose the ability to form words easily. It can happen after a TBI or a stroke. Some people have to be taught how to speak again from scratch. You seem to be doing really well on that front, though.”

“Do I?” Agatha asked, suddenly looking self-conscious.

“Very,” Rio said. “I mean, I pulled you out of the ocean yesterday. Most people struggling with aphasia caused by TBIs and strokes take months to recover. Some even take years. You are extraordinary.”

Agatha smiled at that, and oh. Rio didn’t know that hearts could actually flip in real life. Because that was totally what hers just did.

Neat.

She pressed her tongue into her cheek and breathed through her nose, trying once again to calm herself. She was a professional; she could handle a pretty woman smiling at her, dammit. Even one with sparkling blue oceans for eyes. And pouty lips. And high cheekbones with a dash of sunburn and freckles.

Rio swallowed thickly and looked down at the water, clearing her throat.

“Okay,” she said, “so now you’re going to turn the walker a little bit and follow me to the other end. Slowly, so you don’t fall.”

Agatha scoffed. “I won’t fall,” she insisted, turning the walker a little too quickly and immediately losing her balance, falling face-first into the pool.

“Goddess!” Rio huffed, ducking into the water to rescue her.

Chapter End Notes

Agatha may have overestimated her abilities just a tad...

Chapter 7

Chapter Summary

Agatha and Lilia learn a little bit more about each other

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Chapter Seven

Extraordinary. Rio had called her extraordinary.

This was far from the first time in her life that Agatha had ever been complimented by a pretty woman. But most would say that she was beautiful or intelligent – both of which Agatha knew to be objectively true, so she wondered if they were actually compliments at all.

But extraordinary…well that wasn’t objective at all. That was enough to make her blush and feel the strange kind of fluttering that came with most of her girlhood crushes. That fluttering hadn’t afflicted her in years, though, as she came into herself in her adulthood. She was the one more often approached by others. She was the one pursued, the one given the option to accept or deny advances from potential mates.

Mermaids traditionally mated for life, but that didn’t mean that one couldn’t seek comfort in the arms of one they didn’t see forever with. After all, most mermaids were human-born, and humans didn’t always mate for life, so why should mermaids be held to a different standard?

The leaders didn’t really like this, but they couldn’t do much about it except shake their heads, disapprovingly.

Agatha didn’t know how many partners she’d had over the years, both long-term and temporary ones, but none of them had ever really stuck. A few had tried to control her, had tried to manipulate her out of her hobbies – namely, exploring outside of the Pod. One or two had even threatened to tell the leaders on her.

Or worse. Her mothers.

Agatha had called all of their bluffs, though, and it had all worked out just fine for her. Except when it disqualified her from being a scout rather than a teacher.

As a scout, she would have been permitted to leave the Pod to find human artifacts and bring them back. She could have even potentially gone to the surface to learn more about the modern human world. Sirens were only allowed to go so far as to find abandoned newborns and children to save and bring back to the Pod or even expectant (yet unwilling) mothers who may have been on the brink of giving up their children to the sea.

Both scouts and Sirens were allowed on land, which meant that they could learn how to walk and talk and dress like humans from their training periods.

Agatha hadn’t even begun her training period when she was pulled out of the program for failing to comply with rules that weren’t even actual rules. The leaders just didn’t like it when they couldn’t shove the ‘lesser’ mermaids into their perfect little boxes.

Agatha was never going to fit into a box, anyway.

Because, according to Rio, she was extraordinary.

Walking became easier in the water, especially with the weird contraption that Rio had given her, which mostly held her up as they paced back and forth across a section of the pool that went up to Agatha’s hips. And the fact that falling, while submerging her in water that stung her eyes if she opened them, didn’t result in any grievous injury but rather in Rio’s hands on her as she helped her back to her feet…well, Agatha couldn’t really complain.

She might have fallen one or two – or six – more times than was absolutely, entirely by accident.

But that was nobody’s business but her own.

Rio kept encouraging her with gentle words and hands, telling her how good she was doing, how miraculous it was that she was already walking and talking just twenty-four hours after such a traumatic event. The fact that she got into the water at all, Rio said, was impressive in itself.

Agatha flushed, feeling partly pleased with all the praise and partly guilty for the deception. Rio’s brown eyes seemed to sparkle with a kind of pride in her that felt somewhat undeserved.

Somewhat.

Agatha was still new to this whole walking thing, and the fact that she had caught onto it so quickly was impressive if not entirely miraculous. She definitely deserved the praise for that much alone. And the talking was another thing. Her jaw and tongue still felt wrong without the weight of water in her mouth, but it was getting easier to speak as Rio carried on conversations with her, asking Agatha about herself and if she was feeling okay or if she needed to rest for a while.

Agatha didn’t want to rest until she had gotten this walking thing down, but there came a point where her new legs were beginning to ache in places – it was very much like the ache in her tail when she’d swum too far while exploring outside the pod and had to rest on a rock before continuing on.

There were no rocks to rest on in a pool.

But the ache was starting to become too much.

Thankfully, Rio noticed.

“Getting tired there?” she asked, giving Agatha a sympathetic smile as she wiped some water from her brow. Lilia had called it sweat. “We can take a rest if you want. It’s been nearly forty minutes now.” She looked at a watch on her wrist. “Oof, make that fifty. The session is almost over. A cool-down period is warranted, I think. Come on.” She encouraged Agatha to turn around (without falling) halfway through a lap and guided her back toward the ramp end of the pool. Before they fully emerged from the water, though, Rio had her stop and pulled the aqua walker away from her, leaving Agatha standing alone in the water while Rio placed it back on dry land.

“Okay now,” Rio said, returning a couple seconds later, “would you rather go sit on the bench,” she motioned toward the long seat against the wall, “or float for a bit in the water?”

“Float?” Agatha asked, furrowing her brow.

“Yeah,” Rio said, patiently, “like on your back or something? I think it takes a lot of pressure off of your spine and leg muscles. It’s also very relaxing, I’ve found, for a lot of my patients to just float for the last few minutes of every session. Makes them real zen.” She gave Agatha a small grin and a quirk of her eyebrows.

Agatha shrugged. “Okay,” she said. “I can float.”

Of course Agatha could float. She was a mermaid. But she couldn’t exactly say that. Also, she didn’t actually know if her human form could float quite as well as her mermaid form could, especially on the surface of the water.

She was about to find out.

“Okay,” Rio said, “do you mind if I touch you?” Her cheeks were pink as she reached out, her hands hovering an inch or two from Agatha’s waist. “Just to help you get into position, I mean.”

Agatha’s cheeks matched hers and suddenly she noticed the lack of water in her mouth more acutely than she had even when she first woke up in the hospital the day before. It made it hard to form any words, so she just nodded.

Rio’s hands had been on her pretty much the entire time they paced through the water together, but this time felt different. Rio was somewhat closer to her as the walker was no longer a barrier between them. Her breath was on Agatha’s cheek as she placed one hand on Agatha’s back, encouraging her to crouch down slightly in the water. Then her other arm was under Agatha’s knees.

“Okay,” Rio said, “I’m going to lift you now. Don’t get panicked.”

“Panicked?” Agatha scoffed. “Why would I—” Agatha let out an involuntary squeak as her feet left the ground, her arms automatically going around Rio’s shoulders as the other woman let out a chuckle. Her legs kicked a little bit, and Rio wobbled for a second before anchoring herself more firmly on the ground.

“You good?” Rio asked, giving her that little grin that showed off the gap between her two front teeth, the one that Agatha thought was strangely endearing. Cute, even.

It kind of made Agatha mad for some odd reason.

“I am good,” Agatha retorted, “but why are you holding me?”

“You don’t like to be held?” Rio asked, her eyes widening. “I’m sorry. I can put you do—”

“No,” Agatha said, a bit too quickly. “No, it’s fine. I’m good. Just a question.”

“Right,” Rio said, her cheeks turning pink again as she grinned. “Right. Um, it’s just easier to lay you on your back in the water this way,” she explained. “Straighten out your legs for me?”

Agatha did as requested, and Rio lowered her onto the surface of the water. She let out a soft gasp as her back hit the water, her nails digging into Rio’s shoulders as the other woman loosened her grip on Agatha’s body.

Rio, for her part, didn’t complain or even show any kind of discomfort as she helped Agatha straighten out her body atop the water. Instead, she crouched a bit, lowering herself into the water, and stroked Agatha’s back underneath it.

“It’s okay,” she soothed. “You’re okay. You’re just going to float, remember? I’m right here.” Her voice was smooth and confident and soothed Agatha’s nerves like hot rocks. She found herself relaxing almost instantly, the water surrounding her but never taking her under. She let out a slow, deep breath. “That’s it,” Rio encouraged as her arms fully released Agatha. “Spread out your arms a little bit.”

Agatha let her arms float outward at her sides, the motion causing her body to turn a little bit in the water, her knees hitting Rio’s arm as she stay crouched in the water at Agatha’s side. She kept a gentle hand under Agatha’s back the entire time she floated, following the motion of Agatha’s body as she shifted around in the water.

Agatha had to admit that it did feel nice. She closed her eyes and allowed her body to relax. She had never floated on top of the water like this: she wasn’t allowed. But she would like to do it more in the coming days if this was how Rio usually ended her sessions with other patients. It felt…nice.

Was the word zen correct, like Rio had said?

Agatha had no idea what that meant, but it somehow felt apt to what she was currently experiencing, especially with Rio’s hand on her back, keeping her from sinking too far into the water.

Not that she would have fallen much. The water was only really going up to her knees before Rio helped her lay down in it. Now she felt as though she could drift off like this. It felt almost like being home…

She felt something on her forehead and her eyes popped open just in time to see Rio pull her hand back, her face red and lips pressed together.

“Sorry!” she said. “There was some hair, uh, stuck to your face. I was just, um, moving it for you.” She gave Agatha an awkward smile, and there were those flutters again. They made Agatha feel utterly ridiculous, but she also wanted them never to stop at the same time.

Ugh. Having feelings was embarrassing.

Agatha prided herself on her ability to stay calm and unaffected in her daily life. There were a couple of teachers’ pets in her class (namely, Billy), but she never let them get too close to her. After all, her own mothers had treated her coldly after they’d gotten to know her and couldn’t change who she was, fundamentally, as a person (which was something that really should not happen, in Agatha’s opinion.) If the two women that raised her couldn’t even stand her personality, why would anybody else?

No, keeping others at a distance was for the best.

“I think,” Agatha said, swallowing thickly, “I’m ready to get out now.”

She wasn’t. She liked floating. She liked being so close to Rio.

But Rio was also too close. She needed to get out before she did something very stupid. Like have another feeling.

Gross.

Rio helped her stand back up in the water, her hand brushing over Agatha’s backside and sending tingles down her leg that made it somewhat difficult to keep her balance.

Luckily, Rio caught her with one hand on Agatha’s waist and the other holding her right hand, steadying her in the shallow water. Agatha’s hand wrapped around Rio’s fingers and tensed when her knees wobbled as Rio guided her up the ramp. Rio’s hand tensed on her waist in reaction. Agatha felt more tingles go up her spine as her face warmed, and she tried to ignore them and focus on her steps.

Heel, toe. Heel, toe. Heel, toe.

It took twelve steps to reach the bench with Rio’s help. Agatha felt out of breath by the time she sat down, but she didn’t know if it was solely from the energy she had exerted from simply walking those twelve steps. She didn’t know what else it could have been, though. Lilia had assured her that lungs worked automatically, that she didn’t have to consciously breath in oxygen just as she hadn’t had to consciously breathe in water (though now she had to consciously not breathe in water).

So why did it feel harder to breathe?

“You okay?” Rio asked, standing above Agatha as she reached into the bag Lilia left for her and pulled out a towel. She handed it to Agatha, who gave her a nod of thanks.

“I’m okay,” Agatha said. “Why wouldn’t I be?”

“Because you’re still holding my hand pretty tightly there,” Rio said, shaking their joined hands slightly. “Are you feeling dizzy or lightheaded or something?”

Agatha’s eyes went wide as she stared at their hands for half a second. Their fingers had, at some point, become interlocked. Agatha hadn’t even noticed because they seemed to fit so well together, like…Agatha couldn’t think of an apt comparison, but it felt as though they were two pieces broken apart from one another.

She’d have to ask Lilia the word for that, if there even was one.

“Yoo-hoo!” Speak of the Devil fish. “Sorry I’m late, but there was a line at the grocery store and then I got caught up with a couple of friends on the way back!”

Rio slipped her fingers casually out of Agatha’s grip with one final squeeze and made her way over to Lilia, who was carrying a cup of something brown with a white tube sticking out of it.

A straw, Agatha’s mind supplied. She’d had one in her milkshake at the diner. Milkshakes were not that color, though, Agatha was certain.

“At the café?” Rio asked, snatching the cup from her hand and taking a sip. Then her nose wrinkled and she pulled the straw away from her mouth, sticking out her tongue. “Decaf? What the hell?”

“When have you ever known me to have caffeine after noon?” Lilia asked. “I’d be bouncing off the walls all night!” She took her cup back and strolled toward Agatha. “You ready to go, doll?” she asked.

“But decaf?” Rio huffed. “What’s even the point of that?”

“The point is to teach you a lesson about grabbing food and drinks out of my hand,” Lilia said, raising an eyebrow. “How was your first session?” she asked, turning back to Agatha. “Are your legs feeling a little less like jelly?”

Agatha furrowed her brow. She didn’t know what ‘jelly’ was. Was it like jellyfish? Squishy and sting-y?

“Just say yes,” Lilia whispered, leaning in to give her a hug. “I’ll explain it at home.

“Yes,” Agatha said, louder than was probably necessary. “My legs feel less like j-jelly. They are fully opaque now.”

Lilia let out a peal of laughter, but Rio just tilted her head and gave Agatha a tiny, confused half-smile, her eyes a little squinted. Agatha knew that she had said something wrong, but she wasn’t really sure how to fix it without potentially making the situation worse, so she said nothing at all.

“Well, let me help you up,” Lilia said, “and let’s see that progress, huh?”

She offered Agatha her free hand and pulled her back to her feet, still wrapped in a towel. Her knees wobbled a bit, knocking together, but she was mostly fine. The backs of her legs ached a bit, but Rio had assured her that that was completely normal since her muscles were probably strained from her ‘dip in the ocean’ as she had put it.

Rio grabbed her wheelchair and brought it to her, keeping it a few feet away as Lilia encouraged her to take a few steps to get to it and show her how much progress she had made.

Agatha’s hand clenched around Lilia’s much in the same way it had clenched around Rio’s earlier. She took a deep breath and took one tentative step in the direction of the chair.

She wobbled a little bit, her sore leg straining with the move, but she did not fall. She let out her breath through her nose and brought her other leg to meet the first, Lilia following along at her side. Unlike earlier that morning and the night before, Agatha wasn’t entirely reliant on Lilia to keep her upright.

That was definitely progress, she thought. She took another step.

“That’s it, doll,” Lilia said, squeezing her hand as she stepped forward with Agatha. “You’ve got it!”

“This is incredible,” Rio murmured, looking straight at Agatha. “Nobody has ever recovered this quickly before.”

“She still has a long way to go,” Lilia said, helping Agatha take another step, “but she’s getting there.”

After two more steps, Agatha was able to turn herself and plop down in the wheelchair, feeling out of breath as Rio tapped her shoulders with excitement, congratulating her on her progress.

But Agatha couldn’t be sure that her lack of breath was entirely due to the walking and not at least in some part due to the way Rio’s fingers clenched around her shoulders and the way she stuck her tongue into her cheek as she smiled proudly down at Agatha.

The stupid flutters were back in full force as Lilia said goodbye to her niece, grabbed Agatha’s bag, and wheeled her out of the hospital.

Over the next three days, Agatha continued her sessions with Rio. The two days following the first were in the pool, but then they moved to a smaller, drier room with windows and other weird things that Rio insisted were important for recovery.

Like a pair of elevated metal tubes that she called the ‘parallel bars’ that Agatha was meant to hold onto as she walked the length of them. By that point, walking had gotten easier – mainly because Lilia had insisted that she practice as much as her sore muscles would allow when at home. She understood how difficult it was to learn how to walk, of course, as she’d had to learn as part of her Siren training when she was just a teenager, but she’d insisted that it was best to work out the muscles as much as possible so as to form the habit a lot more quickly.

It was getting easier to walk, Agatha had to admit. And she was able to breathe more smoothly as she walked, too. She still had to stop every once in a while to rub the back of her legs (her calves, Lilia had called them), but she no longer looked like a ‘cute newborn doe’ like Rio had called her when Agatha’s knees had knocked together halfway through the parallel bars the first time out of water.

Agatha had flushed at that. Not because she was being compared to a baby land animal that she’d never seen before and could have been the ugliest creature known to man for all she knew (Lilia had shown her a picture later that day, assuring Agatha that they were indeed very cute), but she’d flushed because Rio had specifically said ‘cute’ and had given her that tongue-in-cheek grin that made Agatha’s knees wobble in the first place.

It had to have been a human thing.

It was also accompanied by that flutter in her stomach. She didn’t dare ask Lilia about that, though, fearing that she already knew the answer and would just end up embarrassing herself.

As new and unfamiliar as everything was on the surface, Agatha couldn’t deny that she was having an objectively good time. Lilia was introducing her to new foods and experiences that she would have never imagined.

There was a building where humans sat for hours on end and watched other humans (who weren’t physically in the room despite appearances) play out entertaining scenarios involving explosions and dramatic declarations of love and confessions while music swelled in the background. Lilia bought her a giant cup (or pitcher?) filled to the brim with a salty treat called ‘popped corn’ and an only slightly smaller cup of something called soda, which was sweet and bubbled on the surface of her tongue with every sip.

And, somehow, that wasn’t considered their supper for the night as Lilia took her a few doors down from the ‘theater’ to a smaller building where they served something called ‘pizza’ which was messy but delicious. They even had anchovies, a little taste of back home. These anchovies were hot on the surface of the pizza, though, and Agatha was encouraged to blow on them to cool them down so that she wouldn’t burn her mouth.

Another night, Lilia had a meal prepared for when Agatha came back from her session with Rio. It was more of the kind of sauce that had been on the pizza, but it was spread over some kind of edible string in a bowl. Atop it sat a few balls of a strange brown meat.

“They’re made of ground beef,” Lilia had explained. “They’re very good.”

“What is a beef?” Agatha asked.

“It’s from a cow,” Lilia informed her. “It’s the same kind of meat that cheeseburger you got from the diner was made of.”

“Oh,” Agatha said. “Well, I liked that, so…”

Agatha really liked the spaghetti and meatballs and was thrilled the next day at lunch when Lilia served her some of the leftovers.

Lilia also had books all over her home. They didn’t see many books in the Pod, and the ones they did see were barely legible as they weren’t made to survive water, so their contents were lost to the sea. Agatha still tried to decipher as much as she could when she found them, but so much of what they contained were human things that she really had no context for.

Lilia’s books, on the other hand, came with Lilia, who could answer the majority of Agatha’s questions even as she went through her usual routines. There were books of animals, books of landmarks, books of maps of places that Agatha had never been before or even knew to explore. There were books of notable humans who had first, last, and even middle names.

“Why don’t mermaids have last or middle names?” Agatha asked, walking into the kitchen one evening after being curled up in one of Lilia’s easy chairs in the study, where there were only books, a few chairs, some dim lights, and what Lilia had called a desk, which was covered in papers and other knickknacks that Agatha couldn’t name but that interested her nonetheless.

“We didn’t feel a need for them,” Lilia explained. “At least as far as I understand it. No two mermaids in the same Pod have the same name.”

“There are other Pods?” Agatha asked, blinking at her.

She didn’t know why the existence of other mermaid pods surprised her. Logically, she knew that they must have existed. Humans existed all over the world, so why shouldn’t mermaids, as well? Especially when so many of the mermaids came from humans.

“They’re not all called Pods,” Lilia said, “but yes, there are more than a hundred other communities. We don’t all exist by the same rules, though. Many of them do have last names. Middle names, too.”

“Can I have a last name?” Agatha asked, her voice quiet, timid.

Lilia stopped what she was doing (preparing something in a pot on the stove for dinner – Agatha was learning so many new words!) and turned fully toward her now.

“You want a last name?” she asked. “Why?”

Agatha shrugged. “I’ve regained my ability to speak,” she said. “And I’ve gotten much better at walking without the use of an aid or a person to help me. Soon enough, Rio and Dr. Vidal are going to question why I haven’t regained my memories. They’ll wonder where I came from, and I won’t be able to tell them the truth, will I? I’ll need a story to give them. At the very least, I’ll need a last name.” She cleared her throat. “Maybe a middle name, as well.”

Lilia considered her for a long moment, then nodded. “Okay,” she said. “You’ve been thinking about this for a minute.”

“An hour, actually,” Agatha said. “This book is full of last names and the people who possess them. They’re all very impressive!” She opened the book to a random page. “Like Nancy Harkness Love: she could fly!”

“With a plane,” Lilia added. “That’s a very important distinction. Humans cannot fly.”

“Obviously,” Agatha huffed. “Still. I like her name.”

“Love? How romantic,” Lilia teased, making a kissy noise at Agatha, who rolled her eyes.

“No,” she said. “Harkness. I like the name Harkness. That was the last name she was given at birth.”

“Interesting name. What do you like about that one?” Lilia asked.

Agatha shrugged. “I just like how it sounds,” she said. “And I think it goes well with my first name. Agatha Harkness: it has a nice ring to it.”

“It does,” Lilia agreed. “And what would you like for your middle name?”

Agatha shrugged. “I’ve never thought this much about names,” she admitted. “I never thought I’d have the chance to name anything, let alone myself. Sirens are the ones that usually do the naming.”

“You never thought about having a child of your own in the Pod?” Lilia asked.

“Biologically unfeasible,” Agatha scoffed. “I’ve never had an interest in any of the few males in our Pod. More than likely, I’d take in one of the landborns like myself. With or without a mate. I just haven’t gotten there yet.”

“Are you waiting for a mate?” Lilia asked, turning back around to stir her pot.

“I…don’t know,” Agatha admitted. “I’m just not there yet. Besides, most of the other mermaids tend to find me…”

“Intimidating?” Lilia guessed

“Bitchy,” Agatha corrected.

Lilia let out a bark of a laugh. “Sorry!” she said. “I just wasn’t expecting that. I cannot believe that the Leaders haven’t outlawed that word yet.”

“They’ve tried,” Agatha said, smiling slightly, “but a few of them have been caught using it, as well. So it didn’t really work out for them.”

“Why do they think you’re bitchy?” Lilia asked, sounding genuinely curious as she continued to stir.

Agatha shrugged. “Because I don’t have patience for stupidity?” Agatha said. “And I don’t try to hide it behind fake politeness. If I think you’re stupid, I’ll usually say it.”

“You’ve never told anybody around here that you think they’re stupid,” Lilia pointed out. “You’ve been perfectly pleasant.”

“I’ve had trouble speaking for the first few days I was here,” Agatha retorted. “Besides that, nobody I’ve interacted with these last few days has been genuinely lacking sense. And nobody has called me stupid for not knowing so many things that are obvious to the vast majority of humans.”

“Well, they’re all under the impression that you have brain damage, doll,” Lilia reminded her. “It would be rude to call you stupid in that case.”

“Still,” Agatha said. “Everybody has been very nice.” Rio’s face flashed in her mind at that, and Agatha felt her cheeks flush.

She glanced up just in time to see the knowing look in Lilia’s eyes before she turned around. She narrowed her gaze at the older woman’s back.

“Why did you decide to stay up here?” she asked.

“I told you that already,” Lilia retorted: “one of my mermaids—”

“Needed your help,” Agatha finished for her. “But why did that mean you had to leave forever? Why couldn’t you come back?”

Agatha wasn’t as hurt as the first time she’d asked Lilia the question, when the sting of rejection wasn’t exactly new but still burned in her chest, nonetheless. Now, having been on the surface for a few days, Agatha could almost understand why Lilia didn’t return to the Pod. There was so much to do on the surface that the Pod just didn’t have. There was still so much for Agatha to see before she returned.

“The girl who needed my help,” Lilia said with a sigh as she turned off the burner on the stove, “was pregnant.”

“Okay…” Agatha said, slowly. “So? She could have had the baby in the sea. She could have provided the Pod with a new Siren.”

“She didn’t want to do that,” Lilia said, turning fully to face Agatha. “For several reasons. One being that the father of her child…wasn’t another mermaid.”

Agatha’s eyes widened at that, and she took a seat on a stool at the counter, placing the book she’d been carrying down. “No…” she said, her voice low. “She mated with a human?”

Lilia nodded, gravely. “She’d been visiting with a human for months at that point. She revealed herself to him when she saved him from drowning after he fell off his boat during a storm. They fell in love and, well, one thing led to another…” She shook her head with a sigh. “The leaders, as you know, are very much against landborn mermaids fraternizing with the humans. She would have been severely punished for breaking one of the rules. Her child would have been taken from her.”

“Why couldn’t she just claim that her baby was that of another mermaid?” Agatha asked, frowning.

“At the time,” Lilia sighed, “we could find none that would be willing to take ownership of the babe. None that could be trusted to keep their mouth shut, anyway. Besides that, she was unwilling to stop seeing the man who fathered her child. She was deeply in love with him.” Lilia smiled softly. “And he was very much in love with her. They wanted to be together, even if that meant that she would have to leave everything she ever knew.”

“But why did that mean you had to leave as well?” Agatha asked, feeling like a whiny child. “Why couldn’t you just drop her off with her human and return?”

Lilia approached the counter and reached across for Agatha’s hand, grasping it before Agatha could pull away.

“I understand why you are upset, doll,” she said. “I do. I wish things could have been different, but this girl…she was so young. She would have been around the same age as your students, just a child in desperate need of help. Her mothers were…difficult. One of them worked under the leadership. She wouldn’t have been able to keep this a secret, even if she wanted to. She needed to get out of there and quick. And somebody needed to care for her up there, to keep her safe. I had a home on land already. I had a way to help her integrate into society.”

“You had a human life here already?” Agatha asked, furrowing her brow. “How come?”

“Many Sirens used to,” Lilia informed her. “We’d keep homes on the surface while we looked for potential…” She pressed her lips together and shook her head.

“Potential what?” Agatha asked after Lilia didn’t finish her sentence.

“Another reason I left,” Lilia said, “was that I didn’t like the practices.”

“Practices?” Agatha asked. “What do you mean?”

“Sirens have songs,” Lilia answered. “We’re known for our voices. Even the humans know our voices. They’ve told stories of them for centuries. The Siren song, luring men to their doom.” She snorted, shaking her head. “We’ve never had that much interest in men. The audacity of them.”

“The Siren songs are meant to provide a beacon for unwilling expectant mother,” Agatha recited. “That’s what we’ve always been taught.”

“That’s what I was taught, as well,” Lilia said. Her hand clenched around Agatha’s. “I believed it for so long, too.”

Agatha stared at their joined hands for a long moment.

“What is the truth?” she asked.

Lilia took a deep breath and gave her a sad smile. “My dear,” she said, “I don’t think you’re quite ready for that conversation yet.” She patted Agatha’s hand. “Please get a few bowls out for dinner; I’ve made us some soup.”

Agatha’s curiosity fought with her as she opened her mouth several times to ask the questions that she so desperately needed the answers to.

What were the songs for if not used to draw out unwilling mothers?

Was the truth really so horrible?

What was so bad that Lilia felt she needed to leave the Pod for good?

The look on Lilia’s face deterred her from asking any of them. Her jaw was clenched, her amber eyes harder than Agatha had seen them since they met, her lips set in a thin line.

Instead, she swallowed those questions down and asked a different one: “What’s soup?”

Chapter End Notes

What is soup indeed?
